    Bootloader & RootFS Redundancy¶

    Phase 4 · Page 1

    Page Goal

    Configure and validate Slot A/B partition redundancy on the NVIDIA Jetson TX2i down to both the Bootloader and the Root Filesystem (RootFS) levels.

    1. Introduction¶

    For operating in extreme environments (such as aerospace or autonomous defense platforms), software single-point failures must be prevented. If a system update fails or a filesystem partition becomes corrupted due to single-event upsets (SEU), the bootloader must automatically fall back to a secondary, known-good boot partition to preserve system availability.

    We implemented A/B slot redundancy at two distinct levels: 1. Bootloader A/B Redundancy: Protects the core booting stages (MB2, Cboot, device trees, BPMP firmware). 2. RootFS A/B Redundancy: Protects the operating system userspace partition.

    Yocto Based Progress

    The RootFS A/B redundancy failover mechanism was validated and tested using a Stock NVIDIA L4T Ubuntu image. A full Yocto-based RootFS A/B integration is currently under development (only bootloader-level redundancy is currently operational in the custom Yocto builds).

    2. Bootloader A/B Redundancy Configuration¶

    We followed the official NVIDIA guidelines and RidgeRun's Jetson TX2 A/B Redundancy Guide to enable slot metadata tracking.

    All modifications are performed from the 18.04 Flashing host's Linux for Tegra (L4T) directory.

    Process Steps to Enable Bootloader A/B Redundancy (from RidgeRun docs)¶

    1. Configuring the Slot Metadata Database (SMD): The configuration files smd_info.cfg and smd_info_rootfs.cfg (located in the L4T bootloader/ directory) define slot priority, boot success flags, and retry thresholds.
    2. Running the SMD Generator: Use the nv_smd_generator utility to parse the config (e.g., smd_info.cfg or smd_info_rootfs.cfg) and generate the binary slot metadata partition package: 
      # Generate slot metadata partition binary
./nv_smd_generator smd_info_rootfs.cfg slot_metadata.bin
    3. Flashing the Redundant Layout: Flash the generated slot configuration to the device. Alternatively, pass the -r option during flashing to rebuild slot allocations.

    Config 1: Disable A/B Support (Default)¶

    By default, the Jetson platform boots with A/B support disabled, marking only Slot A (_a) as active:

    # Set the maximum boot slot retry count
< MAX_BL_RETRY_COUNT 7 >

# slot info order is important!
# <priority>    <suffix>  <boot_successful>
15                  _a        1

    Config 2: Enable A/B Redundancy Support¶

    To enable redundancy, uncomment the parameters to activate Slot B (_b) and configure the redundancy driver:

    # Set the maximum boot slot retry count
< MAX_BL_RETRY_COUNT 7 >

# Config 2: Enable redundancy support
< REDUNDANCY_USER 1 >

# slot info order is important!
# <priority>    <suffix>  <boot_successful>
15                  _a        1
14                  _b        1

    3. RootFS A/B Redundancy Configuration¶

    To enable RootFS-level A/B redundancy, we configure slot metadata variables directly or via compiler flags in the L4T configuration files.

    Configuring RootFS A/B Parameters¶

    The configuration section in the slot metadata configuration file (specifically smd_info_rootfs.cfg) defines unified boot control parameters:

    # Set the maximum boot slot retry count
< MAX_BL_RETRY_COUNT 7 >

# Set the maximum rootfs slot retry count
< MAX_ROOTFS_AB_RETRY_COUNT 3 >

# Config 2: Enable rootfs A/B support (default)
< REDUNDANCY_ENABLE 1 >
< ROOTFS_AB 1 >

# Select rootfs A as the active rootfs
< ROOTFS_ACTIVE_A 1 >

# Enable unified bootloader AB and rootfs AB
< ROOTFS_BL_UNIFIED_AB 1 >

# Disable bootloader autosync to allow manual slot management
< BL_AUTOSYNC_DISABLE 1 >

# slot info order is important!
# <priority>    <suffix>  <boot_successful>
15                  _a        1
14                  _b        1

    Flashing with the RootFS A/B Flag¶

    As documented in Connect Tech Flash Scripts (Phase 2 Page 5), the flashing script is executed using our custom flashing wrapper. To flash a target board with RootFS A/B redundancy enabled, we modified the flashing script cti-flash.sh to accept the environment flag ROOTFS_AB=1:

    # Change the flash command on the host machine targeting Connect Tech Elroy carrier board - inside cti-flash.sh edit the line to
ROOTFS_AB=1 ./flash.sh cti/$2/$BOARD_TYPE/$1 mmcblk0p1
    This forces L4T to layout the eMMC partitions with both APP (Slot A) and APP_b (Slot B) root filesystem slots.

    4. Hardware Testing & Failover Verification¶

    To verify the bootloader and rootfs failover logic, we referred to the NVIDIA Forum RootFS A/B Redundancy Fail-over Guide.

    Test Design & Execution¶

    1. The board was flashed and booted successfully into Slot B (active rootfs suffix _b).
    2. To simulate partition corruption or a broken system update, we corrupted the active partition by deleting the kernel module directory: 
      sudo rm -rf /lib/modules
    3. We rebooted the target board while monitoring the boot sequence over the serial console.
    4. During boot, the Linux kernel initiated a kernel panic because the critical module files and drivers were missing.
    5. The Tegra watchdog / bootloader detected the failure, rebooted the system, and decremented the retry count for Slot B.
    6. Once the slot retry counter was exhausted, the bootloader automatically modified the Slot Metadata Database and selected Slot A (slot 0) as the active fallback boot slot.

    5. Serial Boot Log Analysis¶

    When the system tries to boot using Slot B, the missing library modules trigger a kernel panic, followed by a scheduled hardware reset:

    [    4.559781] Kernel panic - not syncing: Attempted to kill init! exitcode=0x00007f00
[    4.648212] trusty-log panic notifier - trusty version Built: 16:08:32 Jun 11 2024
[    4.664549] Rebooting in 5 seconds..

    Upon reboot, the Tegra bootloader (MB2) initializes and parses the Slot Metadata Database, loading Slot B (slot 1) for the retry attempt:

    [0000.409] I> A/B: bin_type (16) slot 1
[0003.949] I> Active rootfs suffix: _b

    After Slot B repeatedly panics and exhausts its retry budget (MAX_ROOTFS_AB_RETRY_COUNT), the bootloader marks Slot B as unbootable and falls back to Slot A (slot 0):

    [0000.409] I> A/B: bin_type (16) slot 0
[0003.945] I> Active rootfs suffix:

    The active slot suffix becomes empty, pointing the system to the partition APP (Slot A), allowing the machine to boot successfully to a functional userspace environment.
